PAYS TRIBUTE TO ROOSEVELT.
That the former Presidential candidate
of the Democratic party Is most hopeful
for the future success of bis party in na
tional politics, he unhesitatingly admits,
i^the policy of President Roosevelt he
3^v? there is evidence of the changing
feeling of the American public He pays
a high tribute to the executive ability or
Roosevelt and believes that in. his force
ful manner of administering the affairs
of his office the President has done much
toward strengthening the Democratic
forces- JigflÃ&tfnESaÃi
"The developing change in public senti
ment." said he last evening, "augurs well
for the future of the Democratic party.
The very things that were denounced
five years ago as too radical for the com
mon welfare of the people zre now being
taken up by the Republican leaders and
made part of that party's policy. As an
illustration. President Roosevelt is sup
porting a policy, long advocated by my
self, that carries the Government back to
the people. Then there Is the ; matter of
arbitration, that was twice incorporated
in my platforms. Another Important
questien is the regulation of railroads,
wbteh iKe "President Is now endeavoring
to enforce.
*"ThÂ«re has aJso been a noticeable
change of public sentiment In regard to
the future of the Philippine Islands. We
have felt that the Filipinos should be
riven their independence and we have
realized that they can't be held as sub
jects or admitted to citizenship. Indepen
dence is the only thing possible. AH these
questions the Democrats fought out in
Jtmr party and the Democratic Demo
crats eventually gained control of their
parts'. While it is true that the Demo
cratic party received a bit of a setback in
the East this- fall, it is almost certain that
the future will find the party advancing
'..^f * most encouraging manner.

cies so long advocated by the Democratic
party has given encouragement to Demo
crats -throughout the country * and the
signs of progressiveness'are most attrac
tive to Democratic leaders."

ON THE WATER FRONT.
Arrimals for Use of Cruiser; : Gal|t)ria
Object to Being Transpqrled|j
Italians Have Hard Time; in Getting
Cattle on Board War Vessel;
A drove of steers, intended for the
Jt-alien cruiser Calabria, raised a great
Commotion on the water front yester
day morning in front of the Peterson
boathouse at the foot of Folsjm
street. Seve.n big beef animals were
driven down to the dock there yes
terday by as many cowboys. The ani
mals were strong and lusty. They
went through the streets of the city
peacefully enough and submitted to be
driven out on to the dock. But here
they came to a dead standstill. The
men from the Calabria had brought a
barge alongside the floating pontoon
at that place and had put up a nar
rcw gangway from the dock to the
W pontoon, down which they wished'-
Jrive the steers.
The steers refused to go down
the plank. Ropes were tied to the ani
mals' horns by the Italians, who com
menced a vigorous pulling toward the
pontoon, \u25a0while the , cowboys on tlje
dock used all known devices to -push
the animals forward. In the mean
time a crowd of 500 people had gath
ered around the spot to witness the
fun. Among the spectators were a
number of Italians. They enlivened
the proceedings with cries of "Va via,"
â¢\u25a0Guardetevi." "presto" and "vira."
Whether or not the big steer of the
band didn't understand or didn't' like
what the Italians were saying about
him is not known,~but at any rate he
suddenly made a dash down the gang
plank, scattering the Italians on the
pontoon in all directions. \u25a0 He got un
der-such headway that he could not
stop on the pontoon, but . ran - straight
into the bay with a great eplash.
Here he floundered about and would
have drowned but for the rope at
tached to his horns, which was now
securely tied to a pile on the wharf.
After a struggle by the Italians, with
the assistance of innumerable hawsers,
coupled wiUi the suggestions of the
600 people on the dock; the animal was
yanked on to the pontoon and shoved
into the Calabria's barge. The bal
ance of the steers all offered stout re
sistance and kicked and bellowed in a
furious fashion as they were being
- hauled into the barge. They were
landed there after two hours'
*"%*.r& work. From the barge they were
taken into the stream alongside the
warship and hoisted on board -with
out further incident. The Calabria will
sail to-day for Honolulu/
Spend A'lffht on Sand Spit.
A gasoline launch, containing a merry party
of young men and women belonging to Bsl
vedere. spent Saturday night on the sand
\u25a0pit off the northeast point of Terba Buena
Island. . Tfcc party had been over to Oak
land to a concert and were _ returning back
v. Belvedere about midnight, when in round-
Ing the sand spit there they were landed
up hlch and <lry- As it was low tide, the
UuticU had to remain there until high water.
which was 6 o'clock yesterday morning. Then
the launch fio&ted off and the rsuch-tlred
out and woe-lx-gone party started back for the
home port. The next time they go at night
thrjr intend to take a. bay pilot.
Tlburon Anchor* tn Bay.
The fleamer Tuburoa caused â¢ometbing' of
a sensation by coming suddenly to anchor off
Broadway wharf yesterday morning, where
she remained for over an hour. Passengers on
passing steamers and people along the docks
all set up a great wondering as to what the
trouble cocld be. The Tiburon left her dock
at 9:30 a. m., bound for Tiburon. She had
ualy cot & few hundred feet away from
the wharf when cne of hw' rudder - cnalns
gave tc-ay. This left her tmmanaeeAbfc, so
the it once dropped an anchor and . came to
a standstill. A small boat was lowered and,
after an hour's work, the damage was re
paired and the Tiburon proceeded on her way
o.Â» it nothing had happened.

TRADE PROSPECTS STILL FLATTERING.
TRADE conditions last week were largely /a continuation; of
t those of the preceding week.. .The elements: of change : were as
definitely marked, and the! monotony which characterized the
situation for several months had apparently jaeen succeeded |byta
certain .fermentation /affecting almost all; line's , of jsusinessV"T.6 what
development this urisettlement oohf h previoj^VcOTditionsf is drifting: re' 7
mains to be seen, but the exhibit Sffii^S^^^^lSll^^SHSfl
ipra of- trade activity.
I mporters, wholesalers, jobbers and .â¢retailers a 11... over,: the coun
try report^ their different lines active, with the fall demand 'larger,
than usual at this time of the year and expanding. Collections have
shown some improvement during the past fortnight, 'though they,
were easy before, and the week's " failures Svere 206, -against 225 dur
ing the same week last year. The bank cleanngs showed a gain
over 1964 of. 17.5, with most of the large cities in the increase cpl-.
umn, and. the aggregate clearings over . . : â¢ Â«; : .
Labor is riot only well employed/ but 'an actual scarcity is "re
ported in some sections. The railroads. continue to feel" the; lack of
cars wherewith to move the merchandise tendered them, and their
earnings continue to show an increase v oyer the same. time last year;
Lumber and other building materia's are still in heavy demand;
showing no falling off in building, operations. No overproduction
in anything is visible anywhere. In fact, -the larger, lines-are
so generally active that "a leading New. -York .financial house ex-:
claims enthusiastically: "This is a. year of big things. Dividends
have been increased to an extent never before equaled in the history
of the country. The corn crop is^the largest on record and the wheat
crop is also very large. Tl;e cotton crop is moderate, but all these
crops "will be marketed at. satisfactory prices. The- iron and steel
trades are not only very busy, but the prospect for the future is
brilliant, with premiums'being paid for sprompt5 prompt deliveries. Commer
cial trade is large and satisfactory, and the heavy and increasing
railway earnings continue to reflect a great vohmie of traffic/ This
is a most excellent summing up of the situation.
Another recognized financial authority of New York says:
"The Government's "figures justify an increase of something like
20,000,000 bushels to the already record-making. August indication
of corn, while the measure of the August deterioration in ; spring
wheat is shown to have been below 6,000,006 bushels. Cri the basis of
the Government's figures of condition md area the harvest promise
of corn is figured by the trade statisticians at, 2,716,918,000 bushels
and of wheat \ 704,447,000 bushels. The. former volume has never
been exceeded, and the latter but once, namely, by the 748,460,000
bushels representing the 190 1 harvest. The 1904 wheat harvest was
but 552,400,000 bushels. Cotton is leaving our : ~ shores at an un
precedented rate, the official statement for August showing- an Jri
crease in the value of the exports of the staple amounting to's34,
000,000, while the exports for the cotton year ending August 31 were
the largest in volume and in value in the trade's" history. Our gen
eral merchandise export statement is continuing its recent excellent
showing, indicating for the eight months of the calendar year just
ended an' increase of $103,076,445 in the value of bur. imports arid of
$115,149,568 in the export account."
Money hardened during the week, call loans -advancing, to d^/i
per cent, but immediately fell back, showing a continued abundance
of funds wherewith to meet all calls. When it was discovered that
there was plenty of money on hand to meet all requirements an ac
tive demand for stocks sprang up and the market confirmed buoyant. 1
Toward the close of the week it was announced that the Rockefeller
and Morgan interests were arranging the preliminaries for a general
upward movement in stocks, and this Had : *a'furthef v stimulating r cf^
feet on the market, though these announcements may. or* may riot
be true and should always be accepted with more or less caution. It
is very easy for any bull on the stock market, to scatter a Â£ repbrt' like
this broadcast, for it is bound to produce more or less effect on \u25a0.spec
ulative and investment sentiment. An instance of this occurred dur
ing the week/it being predicted in banking circles that the Bank of
England would raise its rate of discount to 4 per cent on Thursday,
and bankers generally made their plans accordingly ; ; but Thursday
came and went and the Bank of England did not 5 raise its rate arid
their plans came to nauglit.
l._-.* The staples are showing more tendency to fluctuate .than for
some time. Raw wool is held so high by the growers that buyers
have withdrawn from the market, and at least, one mill has closed
down because of the fancy quotations asked for wool arid the falling
offrin the, demand for woolen goods. . Hops have" steadily declined
during the past few weeks and are now lower, than for' some time.
Provisions, too, have gone dowii. Per contra/ the- dry goods trade
is so active. that reports from New York say that it is difficult. to sat
isfy all .the orders now being received. Canned fruits and" vegeta
bles are- well cleaned up all over the country and the demand "con
tinues brisk. The market for dried fruits of all kinds is '\u25a0scantily
supplied and very stiff, with prices high, and the. market; has ;ribt
been in such fine "condition for years. Dairy products- and groceries
are also in quick demand as a rule, with. the^ riierchants;manufac
turers and farmers satisfied with current conditions.-
These features make^an excellent exhibit of the condition pf
trade.. We are^ still on the crest of. the Wave of prosperity, and the
9" ! y^estion is how long we. shall be there.

WILL FORMULATE
CAMPAIGN PLANS
MOSCOW, Sept. 24.â Owing to t,fce fact
that there is no danger of police interfer
ence, the congress of xemstvos and mu
nicipal representatix-es, which opens here
\u25a0to-morrow, is attracting less attention
than previous congresses, but the subject
for discussion is extremely important, as
It embraces criticism of the national as
sembly project, which had not been an
nounced when the previous. congress met,
and the formulation of a plan of cam
paign for the ccrnlng elections. *
Though the majority of the delegates
arÂ» apparently willing to accept the as
sembly en the present lines as an earnest
cf further reforms, a strong minority will
present some very sharp criticisms .of the
project. The deputation from Kostroma,
for instance, has been instructed that
the assembly answers neither thÂ« wishes
ncr the needs of the country, and that
elections under the prevailing conditions,
without freedom of assembly or of the
press, are Impossible. _
A resolution will be proposed pointing
out to the Government the imperative
necessity of granting liberty, ci meeting
ar.d of the press immediately if the as
sembly Is to, bÂ« made truly representa
tive. The sentiments of the people havo
been ct-nvassed by the delegates, who.
will present them to the congress, which
will undoubtedly act in accordance with
them.

The Commuters were pretty lucky to
put the Giants out of the running In
the afternoon game yesterday \u25a0< at

bad in his rulings in the fatal Unth
spasm and with the bases all filled and

good-night signal.

muters came up for a final stand. Byrnes
opened it up with a drive over second and
Iberg fanned. Old Rip Van Haltren beat
out his third infield hit ; and a moment
later Essick threw to first to catch Van
napping. Byrnes started on the throw
and slid into third. It looked like Swee
ney had the ball on him, but Perrlne said
"safe." which the multitude hissed.
That was only the beginning , of the
rough work. Kruger was at the'bat and
Esslck had thrown three balls .! to him.

Into the hit that broke up the game. ;i

The Commuters were pretty lucky to
put the Giants out of the running In
the afternoon game yesterday \u25a0< at
Recreation Park. Bull Perlne was
bad in his rulings in the fatal Unth
spasm and with the bases all filled and
one man etowed away, Dunleavy drove
out a single to right field which was the
good-night signal.
The score was one all when the Com
muters came up for a final stand. Byrnes
opened it up with a drive over second and
Iberg fanned. Old Rip Van Haltren beat
out his third infield hit ; and a moment
later Essick threw to first to catch Van
napping. Byrnes started on the throw
and slid into third. It looked like Swee
ney had the ball on him, but Perrlne said
"safe." which the multitude hissed.
That was only the beginning , of the
rough work. Kruger was at the'bat and
Esslck had thrown three balls .! to him.
The fourth curved" right : over the olate
and was a beautiful strike. Here Per
rine was surely wrong, for; he called It a
ball and allowed Kruger, U> .walk, filling
up every sack. r â - : .. -. ~ ... ....
The .Giants stormed around the field and
It looked bad for the umpire. "Atz cursed
and swore louder than any of the others,
so Perrine v promptly chased him off the
lot. Another wrangle followed, but when
Dunleavy stepped to the pan he clouted
the tlrst one that sailed up and it turned
Into the hit that broke up the game. ;i
But for the finish it was* one' grand
ffame of ball. The Commuters .managed
to sneak a run through in the seventh
when Moskiman got as far .as second on
Mitchell's poor , toss to Garvin, who was
covering: first. Richards swung 1 through
to the score board with a triple* and Mos
kiman came all .the I , way home. .
It looked like the Commuters had the
game in till Cates came up and took a
swing at v the . ball In place!, of Garvin . in
the , ninth. Cates -sailed^one. over. ; Van
Haltren's" head "for a"' double" and ' Atz
bunted him v along .to third.. McCreedio
dumped a slow'o'neat Francks,' working
the squeeze play nicely and bringing
Cates in.
Both Iberg and Garvin' pitched the kind
of ball' that l sets the fans wild.' They
fceemed to have everything and, none of
the batters could fall in with any hits'.
The fielding was fast throughout, the;ln
fields of both teams playing superb ball.
Francks gobbled uo ten chances without
falling down once. Oakland finished up
the series by taking four out of the seven
games from the Giants. The. score:
